  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e4717846-6990-4056-ae43-ce2f87623be4'

<span id="freeTextContainer8481297762914670591"><b>Set in an alternate Europe where bloody conflicts rage, the final book of the Crown of Stars epic fantasy series concludes the world-shaking conflict for the survival of humanity.</b><br/><br/>In the wake of the cataclysm that has reshaped the very lands, Sanglant is struggling to legitimize his own rulership and Liath’s status as his wife and consort, even as others are leaguing agains</span>
  <span id="freeText8481297762914670591" style="display:none"><b>Set in an alternate Europe where bloody conflicts rage, the final book of the Crown of Stars epic fantasy series concludes the world-shaking conflict for the survival of humanity.</b><br /><br />In the wake of the cataclysm that has reshaped the very lands, Sanglant is struggling to legitimize his own rulership and Liath’s status as his wife and consort, even as others are leaguing against him….<br /><br />The Aoi are carrying out random attacks on the humans and implicating Sanglant as their leader….<br />While Liath, searching for forbidden magics, is unexpectedly beset by enemies she may not be able to withstand….<br /><br />Stronghand is on a march of conquest that will inevitably lead into the heart of Sanglant’s realm….<br /><br />Adelheid has made an unholy alliance with the treacherous Antonia, who, with the deadly galla at her command, is prepared to strike at Liath, Sanglant, or anyone who threatens her plans….<br /><br />Sabella and Duke Conrad have also marshaled their forces and are moving to seize the crown from Sanglant….<br /><br />And Alain must take his own stand against the Lady of Battles if he is to have any hope of redeeming this war- and magic-torn world….</span>

<div id="review_2691091652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2691091652" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2691091652?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50424456-mayim-de-vries?shelf=avoid-lifes-too-short-for-bad-books">avoid-lifes-too-short-for-bad-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2691091652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9479305428182044235"><b>There is a total grand zero of stars in this *crown*.</b><br/><br/>At this point, all you are interested in is whether or not you <b>should invest your reading time</b> into this series. The answer is: <b>fuck, no! Do not even come near. Unless you come with a <s>torch burner</s> burning torch</b>. (I normally avoid profanities but once in a while there comes a book so obscenely bad that nothing except foul words is fitting).<br/><br/>If you want to know everything that is wrong with this book, just read this <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19255492-crown-of-stars-jan-8-2019' rel='nofollow noopener'>snarky thread</a>. I am not going </span>
  <span id="freeText9479305428182044235" style="display:none"><b>There is a total grand zero of stars in this *crown*.</b><br /><br />At this point, all you are interested in is whether or not you <b>should invest your reading time</b> into this series. The answer is: <b>fuck, no! Do not even come near. Unless you come with a <s>torch burner</s> burning torch</b>. (I normally avoid profanities but once in a while there comes a book so obscenely bad that nothing except foul words is fitting).<br /><br />If you want to know everything that is wrong with this book, just read this <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19255492-crown-of-stars-jan-8-2019" rel="nofollow noopener">snarky thread</a>. I am not going to be going into details here because it would be like <b>wading into a sever</b>. Suffice to say, that Crown of Stars is <b>a strong contender for the worst book of the year</b>, very close to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1957890758?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Core</a> of bad writing and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1988558412?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen of Fire</a> that, <i>ex aequo</i>, won this title the year before. <br /><br /><b>It was so bad, I went back and lowered my ratings of the previous intalments</b>. <br /><br />It is interesting that all three are supposed to be a grand finale in a series. Even more interesting that in all three cases the opening entries were so great that I found myself gushing in the reviews. All three authors were, however, <b>unable to carry out the fantastic ideas and deliver what had been promised</b>. Ms Elliott has fallen the farthest in this respect because her series is the longest and she took the most time writing it. <br /><br />If you told me to read the Crown of Stars back to back with King's Dragon, I would not believe that these two belong together. The shortcuts taken, the total disregard for the initial arcs, the precarious developments along the way that have nothing in common with the intrigue heralded in the first Prologue, surreptitious execution and elimination of elements that did not fit any more (you did not deserve that, O Wise Mothers!), the hughing of Hugh ('unforgivable' is a cuddly way to describe my feelings). <br /><br />Kate Elliott managed not only to destroy both of her protagonists but also her antagonist whose impending and most unpleasant death was one of the few things propelling me onwards. The fact that it never happened is just another example of <b>the Author cheating on her readers</b>.<br /><br />Some of my friends dropped the series after the third instalment. In the hindsight, I need to admit it was a wise decision. Crown of Stars would benefit greatly if somebody edited it heavily, which basically means trimming it down by half at least and amending some of the threads to retain the logic of the main arc. <br /><br />Until that happens, do not bother with this series. I am adding it to the long list of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19544504-top-three-books-you-wish-someone-would-rewrite" rel="nofollow noopener">books I wish someone would rewrite</a>.<br /><br />___<br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451848010?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">King's Dragon</a> ★★★★★<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2482145978" rel="nofollow noopener">Prince of Dogs</a> ★★★★☆<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2524396893?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Burning Stone </a> ★★★★☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568628569" rel="nofollow noopener">Child of Flame</a> ★★★☆☆<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2584893552?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Strom</a> ★★☆☆☆<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2615243002" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Ruins</a> ★☆☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="9479305428182044235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1679375369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679375369" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679375369?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780756403263" href="/book/show/2286291.Crown_of_Stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679375369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14170381210050624374">For those who don’t already know: I am not a series reader. I like my books fresh rather than familiar, and even a trilogy is a lot of one story for me. Half the reason I read this saga is because I enjoy Elliott’s work and find it remarkably consistent in quality (I tire of authors as quickly as I tire of series, but after a whopping 15 books from her, am still looking forward to the next installment of Black Wolves). The other half was just to have the experience of reading a 7-book fantasy se</span>
  <span id="freeText14170381210050624374" style="display:none">For those who don’t already know: I am not a series reader. I like my books fresh rather than familiar, and even a trilogy is a lot of one story for me. Half the reason I read this saga is because I enjoy Elliott’s work and find it remarkably consistent in quality (I tire of authors as quickly as I tire of series, but after a whopping 15 books from her, am still looking forward to the next installment of Black Wolves). The other half was just to have the experience of reading a 7-book fantasy series. Aside from Harry Potter and Narnia, I believe this was a first.<br /><br />And I was glad to be done with it, because after the third book it started to get stale (lovers of long series may feel differently). The characters are not really that deep or exciting, and a lot of pages are spent on fairly flat secondaries. The plot loses momentum; every once in awhile there’s a chance to blow everything open and get some real action going, but while it never bogs down like certain other series (I read most of the Wheel of Time, okay, can you blame me for not wanting more?), it just sort of trundles along in the later books, without much sense of danger and urgency and the fate of the world – or at least our favorite characters – resting on a knife edge, which is what you want in epic fantasy. As for this last volume, it isn’t bad, but nor was it an edge-of-the-seat read. Many of the subplots to which much time was devoted over the course of the series still don’t seem essential.<br /><br />The ending itself is decent. Not having a definitive resolution to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the return of the Ashioi <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is unusual and anticlimactic, though much more realistic than your typical fantasy (after all, real foreign relations are rarely settled once and for all). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The villains get their just desserts (I’m surprised at the comments that they get off lightly, and after reading them was expecting Hugh or Antonia to get off scot-free). Liath and Sanglant get their happy ending (so after dying and coming back, Sanglant no longer wants to be king? Convenient). Alain wanders off into the sunset with his dogs (inconclusive, but in this character’s transition to sainthood, he felt more and more distant to this reader, to the point it’s hard to envision anything else). Rosvita is elected the new skopos (the perfect ending for this dull paragon of a character). And Hanna hooks up with Ivar (she’d definitely outgrown and outclassed this whiny dude, who was clearly in a relationship with his male best friend anyway. These two never even had chemistry). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All in all, a fine ending to a series I’d have liked better as a trilogy. Elliott’s writing has improved and her series grown shorter since, and thank goodness for that.<br /><br /><br />Crown of Stars ratings:<br /><br />King’s Dragon: 4<br />Prince of Dogs: 3.5<br />The Burning Stone: 4<br />Child of Flame: 3<br />The Gathering Storm: 2.5<br />In the Ruins: 3<br />Crown of Stars: 3</span>
  <a data-text-id="14170381210050624374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1507798890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507798890" />
    <a title="Teleseparatist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3526766-teleseparatist"><img alt="Teleseparatist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528998170p2/3526766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507798890?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teleseparatist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teleseparatist" href="/user/show/3526766-teleseparatist">Teleseparatist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19833203-crown-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3526766-teleseparatist?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3526766-teleseparatist?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507798890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7634494163895628292">Looks like I made it! After many months of reading volume after volume, I'm done with this series. <br/><br/>By the end, it felt slightly bloated. I wish some storylines had been cut, and yet, oddly enough, the ending felt slightly rushed. Still, it was a fantastical journey, a true epic and an amazing series full of characters I loved, got annoyed by and hated. I almost threw the book across the room more than once (in a good way, mostly). I developed in-jokes with my SO about the book. I'll miss having </span>
  <span id="freeText7634494163895628292" style="display:none">Looks like I made it! After many months of reading volume after volume, I'm done with this series. <br /><br />By the end, it felt slightly bloated. I wish some storylines had been cut, and yet, oddly enough, the ending felt slightly rushed. Still, it was a fantastical journey, a true epic and an amazing series full of characters I loved, got annoyed by and hated. I almost threw the book across the room more than once (in a good way, mostly). I developed in-jokes with my SO about the book. I'll miss having more Kate Elliott fantasy to read. (When is the next novel???)<br /><br />The ending was (mostly) satisfying and as sweeping as Elliott is capable of. <br /><br />And yet, I find myself frustrated by this book, so much. There are things that disappointed me so bad. Knowing Kate Elliott's feminism from her other novels, knowing how right she is in her meta on the subject of representation... I was terribly disappointed on several counts. <br /><br />Spoilers about these issues below the cut.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />There was one implied-lesbian character. She died. And there was a joke about her possibly raping women.<br />There was one "two spirit" / trans woman character. She was presented as "not male or female" for the purposes of a curse (which was basically the only narrative reason for her appearance in the novel) and guess what? She died.<br />There were several characters who are identifiably of colour. The following list includes most of them: One of them, it turned out, wasn't really a person of colour by human ancestry, she was half-white, half-daimonic. One was forcibly married at a very young age and died on page. One was brutally murdered on page. And two were, well, rapists (that's Conrad and Sorgatani by the way).<br /><br />I hated that the resolution to Hanna's storyline is her getting together with Ivar. They apparently have some magical connection because she had many much nicer dudes hitting on her to no avail, but she sees Ivar after ages and it's instant-kissing. Perhaps I'm forgetting something from book 1 that would make this match better, but honestly, I disliked Ivar and his privileged assholery all along, and to have him be an Eagle doesn't suddenly redeem him. Hanna's entire storyline was about wanting to see the world -&gt; being traumatised by what she saw -&gt; ending up getting together with a guy from her village. Sure, they'll travel together. It doesn't make it any less disappointing.<br /><br />And then there's Sorgatani, who can't meet a guy who will love her enough to be her pura without it being terribly gross. No, instead she chooses to make Hugh her slave / sex slave. Because apparently two wrongs make a satisfying conclusion. I'm not sure if I'm more opposed to the notion that it's just desserts because he was a rapist (and rapist's son), or disgusted by the idea of him ever having relations of any type with Sorgatani. She deserved better than to be his punishment and diminished by that function. <br /><br />I still loved the books. I loved them a lot. But it wasn't right. I know my frustration is not with Kate Elliott's novels only. It's with how little representation lesbian women, and women having sex with women, and bi women, get in fiction. But all the same, these books had several plotlines with gay guys. There are Swordspoint novels and now a serial. People swoon about Malec on TV. And lesbians get to have one character who dies. (And I know there are f/f plots in Black Wolves. Guess what, I didn't like them. :/)<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My SO remarked that a lot of Crossroads could work as an AU for this novel (what if Sanglant decided to turn Liath aside to have a proper wife for dynastic reasons?). I'd be curious to read about the connections. But a part of me wishes all those Kate Elliott books could be slightly less grim :(<br /><br />(Well, I'll always have Spiritwalker. Although its ending has its shadows as well.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7634494163895628292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6820202551908369876">Absolutely amazing ending! Everything was tied together spectacularly, and I was so astounded after finishing this that I couldn't sleep! I distinctly remember blurting, "Oh. My god," several times in the last several chapters. By the time I placed the finished book on my shelf, I was probably in shock.<br/><br/>The ending was wonderful. It really was. I couldn't have asked for better. <br/><br/>This series was well worth the read, and I have to say will probably take the place of Wheel of Time as my favorite book </span>
  <span id="freeText6820202551908369876" style="display:none">Absolutely amazing ending! Everything was tied together spectacularly, and I was so astounded after finishing this that I couldn't sleep! I distinctly remember blurting, "Oh. My god," several times in the last several chapters. By the time I placed the finished book on my shelf, I was probably in shock.<br /><br />The ending was wonderful. It really was. I couldn't have asked for better. <br /><br />This series was well worth the read, and I have to say will probably take the place of Wheel of Time as my favorite book series ever. I'll definitely be able to reread these books in the future, and will be excited to catch all those scattered clues I didn't notice before. <br /><br />Despite what any early readers may think, Alain's storyline is the best. I don't care who you are. Out of everything that happened in the last couple of books, scenes with Alain were what elicited the strongest reactions from me. I teared up twice at the end, and gasped, and exclaimed, and I honestly think Alain was the best character. <br /><br />I don't really understand the negative reviews at all, from people who couldn't finish the books. I never once got bored. I never once wanted to quit. And I'm a very picky reader. The Crown of Stars was everything I ever could've hoped for in a series. The character development was PERFECT. Characters you didn't like at first become so well-rounded. Even the horrid beast Wichman was, by the end, someone that I was rooting for. Kate Elliott did so well with this series. I can't even properly explain how perfect every perspective and subplot was. The way everything came together, the way it all ended... just amazing. AMAZING. </span>

<div id="review_3478398489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3478398489" />
    <a title="Edward Rathke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5657249-edward-rathke"><img alt="Edward Rathke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442510992p2/5657249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3478398489?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Rathke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Rathke" href="/user/show/5657249-edward-rathke">Edward Rathke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5657249-edward-rathke?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3478398489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10093924669341421998">After seven books, I don't actually have that much to say. Which is weird! Because usually this is where I write sort of a meta-review.<br/><br/>This book did manage some surprises, but I don't think any of the surprises are that interesting. Or, they could have been, but Elliott sort of steers us away from those interesting elements, as she always seems to. <br/><br/>I would say I'm largely unhappy with the resolutions of the novel, though I don't think they're necessarily bad. But they are just so...vapid.<br/><br/>This se</span>
  <span id="freeText10093924669341421998" style="display:none">After seven books, I don't actually have that much to say. Which is weird! Because usually this is where I write sort of a meta-review.<br /><br />This book did manage some surprises, but I don't think any of the surprises are that interesting. Or, they could have been, but Elliott sort of steers us away from those interesting elements, as she always seems to. <br /><br />I would say I'm largely unhappy with the resolutions of the novel, though I don't think they're necessarily bad. But they are just so...vapid.<br /><br />This series was always best, to me, when Elliott kept her distance from the royals but as the series progressed it became more and more wrapped up in the bickering of princes and bishops. And then the resolutions are essentially that everyone ends up becoming a royal of some kind or at least pulled into the direct sphere of a royal. <br /><br />Even so, there are a lot of great moments in here and I do genuinely like many of the characters. So I'm not really disappointed, but this series--<br /><br />It just never managed to be what I thought it could be. Elliott showed so much potential and leaned into some very interesting ideas and dynamics, but then kind of tossed it all into a blender with generic epic fantasy elements and what we end up with is an above average epic fantasy series that sort of feels like you've already read it.<br /><br />I don't know. I liked it all well enough, but I'm glad to be done with it. I also can't imagine recommending this to anyone, since I think the things it does well aren't really enough to distinguish it from other epic fantasy series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10093924669341421998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2458096717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2458096717" />
    <a title="Clay Kallam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/961119-clay-kallam"><img alt="Clay Kallam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315492109p2/961119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2458096717?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clay Kallam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clay Kallam" href="/user/show/961119-clay-kallam">Clay Kallam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/961119-clay-kallam?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2458096717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14233328830756338510">(This review is of the Crown of Stars series, not the individual books, but is attached to each one so that potential readers know what they’re getting into. It is imperative to begin with “King’s Dragon,” of course, and once involved, the difference in quality and focus of each of the seven volumes is far less important than the impact of the series as a whole.)<br/><br/>Crown of Stars is a sprawling, sometimes confusing, seven volumes of epic medieval fantasy that is worth the investment of time and ene</span>
  <span id="freeText14233328830756338510" style="display:none">(This review is of the Crown of Stars series, not the individual books, but is attached to each one so that potential readers know what they’re getting into. It is imperative to begin with “King’s Dragon,” of course, and once involved, the difference in quality and focus of each of the seven volumes is far less important than the impact of the series as a whole.)<br /><br />Crown of Stars is a sprawling, sometimes confusing, seven volumes of epic medieval fantasy that is worth the investment of time and energy to track its multitude of characters through complex plots and subplots as they battle their way through 4,000 pages of magic, catastrophe and of course, eventual redemption.<br /><br />But first it has to be said that Kate Elliott doesn’t bring every one of her characters all the way home, as more than a few are killed relatively early in the series, and some that seem destined for an early demise just keep hanging on. This kind of uncertainty, and some unexpected plot twists, keep the pages turning, and makes this long series an entertaining and worthwhile ride.<br /><br />The setup is a thinly disguised medieval Europe (think 9th century) a few generations after the death of Charlemagne (called Taillefer in the book). The echoes of the Dariyan (read “Roman”) Empire still linger, but the political side of the book is concerned with the dynastic maneuverings of Central European dukes and kings, which are complex to begin with and get even more so as the books roll on.<br /><br />The fantasy aspect combines powerful magic wielded by a minority of humans, plus some non-human races (though the Eika are the Vikings) and cosmology that resembles the ancient Greek theories about the spheres of existence that surround Earth.<br /><br />And then of course there are the human interactions, ranging from obsession (both love and hate), religious fervor, lust for power, and revenge, all played out through a cast of what seems like thousands. (Keeping track isn’t all that easy, and when Elliott wraps everything up, it’s not a simple task to sort everything, and everyone, out on just one reading.)<br /><br />Though there are many point-of-view characters, probably the two most important are Liath, a young woman who has spent her life running away from something her father greatly fears, and Alain, a young farm boy who draws the attention of powerful humans and spirits.<br /><br />But almost equally important are Sanglant, a bastard son of King Henry whose mother is a mysterious Aoi (perhaps human, perhaps just slightly different); Rosvita, a nun and advisor to King Henry; Ivar, a young nobleman; and Stronghand, a young Eika warrior.<br /><br />There are plenty of villains, fully fleshed out minor characters, a magical catastrophe, and most important in works as long and complex as this one, a satisfying ending.<br /><br />The Crown of Stars, all in all, is an excellent medieval fantasy, though not quite up to Miles Cameron’s Traitor Son Cycle (which was written after this) and perhaps a little too complicated for its own good. And naturally, some of the seven volumes are better than others, but if “King’s Dragon” grabs your interest, then go ahead and buy the other six – you’ll have thousands of pages of enjoyment ahead, and the luxury of knowing that you have months of good reading on the way.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14233328830756338510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13283207622519945693" style="display:none">Book VII<br /><br />A few months following the cataclysm, Liath, Sanglant, Alain, Stronghand and many others are trying to right the land that they love and come from.   <span id="freeText6239598971207964797" style="display:none">Overall, good. I could not put it down until I read every word within every book of this series. The 6th book was, by far, the worst, and this last installment demonstrated a vast improvement. I especially enjoyed that some likable characters die and that some "villains" live. I don't like endings to be too soppy and "feel-good" and Ms. Elliott does pretty well with that. I really enjoyed her descriptives, except where the astronomy is elaborated on. I know that it is somewhat important to the saga, but I could stand a bit less of it and tended to skim those parts. I am amazed that someone is capable of creating such an intricate plot and write it so well. I liked that she wrote in third person, yet changed points of view regularly. I did not like that several things were repeated many times throughout the entire series.</span>

<div id="review_2213822314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2213822314" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2609984-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522664318p2/2609984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2213822314?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2609984-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2609984-rebecca?shelf=skimmed">skimmed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2213822314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17076622277502054444">As the books progressed, I read less and skimmed more... I love Kate Elliott's books (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20980680.Black_Wolves__Black_Wolves___1_' title='Black Wolves (Black Wolves, #1) by Kate Elliott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black Wolves</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7114825.Cold_Magic__Spiritwalker___1_' title='Cold Magic (Spiritwalker, #1) by Kate Elliott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cold Magic</a>, etc) so I am reading her older books and well... I guess every author has to start somewhere, and this series is kinda weak. I'm leery/skeptical of any series that goes beyond three books (except Kate Daniels), because it starts getting bloated and lackluster... and this series felt like that as it moved on. <br/><br/>I did enjoy the first book though. It seemed like a pretty solid/promising sta</span>
  <span id="freeText17076622277502054444" style="display:none">As the books progressed, I read less and skimmed more... I love Kate Elliott's books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20980680.Black_Wolves__Black_Wolves___1_" title="Black Wolves (Black Wolves, #1) by Kate Elliott" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Wolves</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7114825.Cold_Magic__Spiritwalker___1_" title="Cold Magic (Spiritwalker, #1) by Kate Elliott" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Magic</a>, etc) so I am reading her older books and well... I guess every author has to start somewhere, and this series is kinda weak. I'm leery/skeptical of any series that goes beyond three books (except Kate Daniels), because it starts getting bloated and lackluster... and this series felt like that as it moved on. <br /><br />I did enjoy the first book though. It seemed like a pretty solid/promising start. But I think as the series progressed and the scope expanded, I started to lose investment. It takes effort for me to become interested when there are three or more narrating characters. Still, it's interesting to see the earlier Kate Elliott books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17076622277502054444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23729668?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23729668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7427018668711493624">**Slight spoiler alert for those who haven't finished Vol. 5**<br/><br/>This was a nice series. After Elliott brought the Aoi land "safely" back to its starting place, one of the major plot arcs drew to a close, and I wasn't sure how she was going to maintain a satisfactory urgency and mystery from that point on. While I don't think that this book has quite the excitement and interest that the first ones did (it gets a bit long-winded sometimes, and Elliott spends a lot of time on needless details, in my </span>
  <span id="freeText7427018668711493624" style="display:none">**Slight spoiler alert for those who haven't finished Vol. 5**<br /><br />This was a nice series. After Elliott brought the Aoi land "safely" back to its starting place, one of the major plot arcs drew to a close, and I wasn't sure how she was going to maintain a satisfactory urgency and mystery from that point on. While I don't think that this book has quite the excitement and interest that the first ones did (it gets a bit long-winded sometimes, and Elliott spends a lot of time on needless details, in my opinion) it's still quite good. The lives of the characters we care about are, for the most part, nicely wrapped up, not so tidily that it feels trite, but enough so that one feels satisfied. All in all, I'd recommend this series to people I know for sure love fantasy, and don't mind spending lots of time reading and getting immersed in interesting worlds. I probably wouldn't recommend it to people with short attention spans, or who want quickly-paced, concise plots.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7427018668711493624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11320051083386922940" style="display:none">I loved this series, and thought the first 5 books were really well done, though I could have done without POVs like Ivar.<br /><br />More Alain and Stronghand would have been great. Alain also became a kind Robin Hobb Fitz character, i.e. what ELSE could happen to the poor man? Also too much repetitive capturing of Liath, and the whole phoenix/religious plot-line became rather boring and far too extensive to me. She should have stuck with only three or four main characters and at times the story felt all over the place.<br /><br />Otherwise it was a great idea and a great story, although it had some flaws.<br /><br />The 6th book was really meh, and although she tied up the many different plot lines nicely in this last book, I didn't enjoy it as much as the earlier books. Still a good ending to a great series!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer15432107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10066356999310322209">Fantasy, last in the Crown of Stars series. The sweeping conclusion: though the world is riven and ravaged, the royal rivals continue fighting over the throne. The wave that has been building through the series crests and breaks in one last, great, bloody battle, after which we are given just enough hints to be sure that most of the protagonists lived happy lives. Conclusive, but rather hastily so considering the sheer bulk of the books that preceded it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer147760826075523978">This was a really an enjoyable end to the series. All of the loose ends were tied up and showed what happened to all of characters which I liked as I had grown close to them with each novel.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1773288317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773288317" />
    <a title="Rindis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/145461-rindis"><img alt="Rindis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182468953p2/145461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773288317?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rindis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rindis" href="/user/show/145461-rindis">Rindis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780756411930" href="/book/show/27405696-crown-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/145461-rindis?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773288317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14017294999745375597">The final volume of Kate Elliot's Crown of Stars series has a lot of work to do. The cast has grown enormous, multiple threats are coming at the main characters from completely different sources, and the political situation is a shambles.<br/><br/>And she pulls it off excellently.<br/><br/>This isn't just a big 'lets smash everything into each other' ending (though there is a battle that largely does that). Instead, there are some very good bridges across technically separate storylines that serve to advance the pl</span>
  <span id="freeText14017294999745375597" style="display:none">The final volume of Kate Elliot's Crown of Stars series has a lot of work to do. The cast has grown enormous, multiple threats are coming at the main characters from completely different sources, and the political situation is a shambles.<br /><br />And she pulls it off excellently.<br /><br />This isn't just a big 'lets smash everything into each other' ending (though there is a battle that largely does that). Instead, there are some very good bridges across technically separate storylines that serve to advance the plot. Moreover, the process of bringing things to a conclusion, brings in, and explains, things that have been in the story since the first book.<br /><br />There <em>are</em> problems. There are (reasonably large) threads that still feel unnecessary to the series as a whole. But everything generally wraps up well, with a decided sense 'this is not the end', but still with an end to the tumultuous events of the last decade.<br /><br />An interesting bit is that the original two main characters of the series, Liath and Alain, have a good understanding and mastery of who they are now, and spend these last two books leveraging their abilities. But Liath, the half-human one, stays essentially human throughout, and her position the series' best character, while Alain basically becomes a force of nature.<br /><br />There are two large questions I still have: Why does the shift of religion from Translatus to Redemptio <em>also</em> shift God from an equal Male and Female duality to a Mother and Son model? And what makes Taillifer so special? Certainly, he's this world's Charlemagne, and <em>politically</em> that is going to be important, but I don't see why the Seven Sleepers were so insistent that they needed a descendant of his for their plans.<br /><br />As a whole, though, <em>Crown of Stars</em> is not only a very good epic fantasy series, but a better, and much more tightly written one, for all its sprawl, than the 'big two' of the last twenty years, and the best one I've seen since <em>Memory, Sorrow and Thorn</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14017294999745375597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3308040592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3308040592" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25992143-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3308040592?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/25992143-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3308040592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6272349568759610166">This historical fantasy put me in mind of George R. R. Martin’s A Song of Ice and Fire. Everyone wanted to be crowned regnant, whether for selfish or noble reasons. Across the seven books, we see the battles and political manoeuvring play out as the possible candidates struggled to gain power. <br/><br/>I enjoyed it at the beginning but this fizzled out around book 5. In general, the problem with A Crown of Stars is one that is common to other Long series - It seemed to go on forever and ever and there we</span>
  <span id="freeText6272349568759610166" style="display:none">This historical fantasy put me in mind of George R. R. Martin’s A Song of Ice and Fire. Everyone wanted to be crowned regnant, whether for selfish or noble reasons. Across the seven books, we see the battles and political manoeuvring play out as the possible candidates struggled to gain power. <br /><br />I enjoyed it at the beginning but this fizzled out around book 5. In general, the problem with A Crown of Stars is one that is common to other Long series - It seemed to go on forever and ever and there were some POVs that simply were not particularly interesting. Towards the middle, I began to feel some series fatigue and for that reason, I would rate this as an overall four star series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6272349568759610166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2900250276" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2900250276" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6381823-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456344459p2/6381823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2900250276?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/6381823-mark">Mark</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2900250276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1863215543925399511">This concludes a very long fantasy series that I found unique and engaging. Most long series that I have read seem to flag and lose focus as they progress as if the author got bored of writting them. This series is an exception. I was carried forward with each well crafted sentence and never found any skackness in the narrative. I intend to read more of Elliott's work in anticipation of hours more introgure and enjoyment.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fbccE/DbgFOFjlDHrJfmL+b7nsRXjufjXUjjs+k0SErJ+ClD6d0oBdNUZgXie0AgaBPeiPdMJjdiu4QahInfCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dcDBHzoDKWcKBjciC7OqbHVopAxIdjJAPmGq+wvEE0nBj/RPIwWBMVzcAeBFXwxj+4DkQOi085QBks1SZnmECg==')})
  }

In the days and weeks that followed, Fang Fang\'s nightly postings gave voice to the fears, frustrations, anger, and hope of missions of her fellow citizens, reflecting on the psychological impact of forced isolation, the role of internet as both community lifeline and source of misinformation, and most tragically, the lives of neighbors and friends taken by the deadly virus.\n\nA fascinating eyewitness account of events as they unfold, \'WUHAN DIARY\' captures the challenges of daily life as changing moods and emotions of being quarantined without reliable information. Fang Fang finds solace in small domestic comforts and is inspired by the courage of friends, health professionals and volunteers, as well as the resilience and perseverance of Wuhan\'s nine million residents. But, by claiming the writer\'s duty to record she also speaks out against social injustice, abuse of power, and other problems which impeded the response to the epidemic and gets herself embroiled in online controversies because of it.\n\nAs Fang Fang documents the beginning of the global health crisis in real time, we are able to identify patterns and mistakes that many of the countries dealing with the novel coronavirus have later repeated. She reminds us that, in the face of the new virus, the plight of the citizens of Wuhan is also that of citizens everywhere. As Fang Fang writes: &quot;The virus is the common enemy of humankind; that is a lesson for all humanity. The only way we can conquer this virus and free ourselves from its grip is for all members of humankind to work together.&quot;\n\nBlending the intimate and the epic, the profound and the quotidian, <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14999833713158415974">As a child in rural Oregon, Kate Elliott made up stories because she longed to escape to a world of lurid adventure fiction. She now writes fantasy, steampunk, and science fiction, often with a romantic edge. She currently lives in Hawaii, where she paddles outrigger canoes and spoils her schnauzer.<br/><br/><br/><br/></span>

But she has let Antonia proclaim herself the new skopos, the Holy Mother who rules over all of the church.
